This places was wonderful. There's something that you just can't fake about a family owned business that cares. The gentleman that took my order was kind and attentive. <UserId.>110320022143456252516<//UserId.>< Name>
S. Anderson<//Name>
<Date>1492916756247</Date>< Rating>
5</Rating>
<Review>For the last two months I've been walking right by this little cafe thinking it was another in a growing line of emerging, commercialized, *meh* quality Indian fast food restaurants.  Knowing that the best Indian restaurant in Monterey was only 5 blocks away, I could not be bothered to spend my money there.

Boy was I surprised.

Today, I found myself hungry and caught in the 2:00-5:00 black hole of restaurant closure.  Not willing to succumb to the pressure of Subway, I decided to give Saffron a try.

My assumptions were SO wrong!

First of all, it is not Indian.  It is an organic, vegetarian, Persian cafe whose quality is on par with Bay of Pines.  (If Bay of Pines was Persian and into the order-and-go market, they would be Saffron).

Second of all, I spent less than I usually do at any of the other fast food places in the Alvarado area (i.e.: Taco Bell, Subway, Round Table, etc).  For the same cost as a meatball sub meal, I got a rather large falafel panini with cucumber salad and cardamom tea.

If you can't see the difference between those two meals...please, just go to McDonalds.

I often whine about my fast food consumption and justify it with an excuse of availability.  Unless I want to brave the Trader Joe's parking lot (*üò±*), getting an organic, cost effective, quick, wholesome meal is impossible.

Saffron remedies that problem.  Given their availability on the Yelp 24 ordering app, all I could do was ask myself:  "What the **** was I doing wasting my money on crap?"

Everything we tried was exceptional: falafels, hummus, yogurt mint cucumber dip, falafel panini, oven baked vegetables (carrots, cauliflower, brussel sprouts, tomatoes, etc), walnut stuffed dates, baklava, cucumber infused water and a rice dish I can't name.

Everything was better than anything I could find on Alvarado...or Cannery Row for that matter.

So, if you are looking for  excellent, culturally rich, healthy, organic food that's priced comparably with the usual fast food restaurants; Saffron is your place and we need more of it.< /Review>< pics>

<review>August 2016: Had a terrible experience with the kids tennis class' instructor Jana Acri. Not only her classes were extremely boring for a 5 year old kid (she had them take turns jumping on the floor ladder for half the class!), she was rude, and a borderline bully as an instructor. Her teaching instructions were not clear and when kids failed to follow her instructions, she kept saying that they need to pay attention, asserting various sorts of "punishments" on them, like sending them to the back of the line without taking a turn at whatever exercise they were doing.

My son told me that day that he hated tennis. Since we quit her class mid-session I've met several other parents who told me that they had a similar experience with that coach.

June 2017 UPDATE: : Raised my review from 1 to 5 stars to reflect updated experience. For the past 10 months my son has been taking tennis classes outside of Broadstone Racquet Club since the club only has 1 instructor that teaches 4-6 years old age range and we didn't want to go back to her. However, a few weeks ago we were able to put him into the next age range group (7-9 years old) class and that experience has been wonderful. His new coach Dennise Chauvet is really great. She has the perfect (for us!) balance of praise/discipline and techniques/games. Calm and professional, Dennise has her students' attention and respect. We are very happy with our tennis situation now and are grateful to another great coach at the club, Alejandro LaCruz, who was extremely helpful in finding a solution for our family so that we can all enjoy our tennis at the Broadstone Racquet Club.

Thanks to Dennise and Alejandro, we are now fans:)))<//review><Gmap_id>0x809ae5ad929d85df:0xd975a8d0ee60c9f9< /Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

<userid>101166001823513538697< /userid><Name>Andrew Baggetta< /Name>< Time>
1556839683728</Time>
<Rate>5<//Rate><Text>This small but welcoming establishment doesn't appear to be much else besides a small town purveyor of Asian cuisine, which they are, however the food speaks to something more going on here.

As other reviews will tell you, the service is great, and every single review that says that is absolutely correct. Service with a smile; good, but light conversation; and beverage upkeep made sure I never was without a crisp, refreshing glass of mint-citrus-apple infused water. I'd come back again just for the water, it's really that good.

Then we get to the food. My whole table was given egg drop soup to start with. A small, humble appetizer that was seasoned really well and had me draining the bowl in seconds. I then ordered a lunch special combination plate. All plates come with white sticky rice and a small, simple salad. Then you get two choices of entrees, of which I opted for yellow curry and Thai Grilled pork. The curry might be the best curry I've had from a small town place like this. The soup on its own was so flavorful, but add to it well cooked and seasoned chicken (the protein option I went with, but they also have beef, pork, and tofu), and hearty cuts of vegetables, and you've got yourself a real good curry going. The good times didn't end there, as I found myself marveling at the flavor and tenderness of the Thai Grilled pork. Cook just right in thin fillets served sliced, it was a fantastic balance of sweet and savory, with a hint of bitterness to cut through it coming from the char the grill provided.

The time spent here was an overall pleasant and surprising experience, one that garnered a high rating and a family of repeat customers; even if it's only for the water.<//Text>< Pics>

<GmapID>0x80db1b11c168e8c9:0xc1e390494da3ec9b<//GmapID>< text>
My stay at Knights Inn was great! Nothing too fancy or luxury but good value for money and has pretty much all the basics you need in a hotel. The bed was super comfy with 4 power outlets on each side of the bed. Air conditioned and a big TV with basic cable, free WiFi too. The bathroom had a separate shower. I couldn't figure out the hot /cold situation but luckily the bath tub also had a shower head that I could figure out. Good water pressure. The kitchen had a fridge, microwave and basic coffee maker. No cutlery or plates/bowls (only plastic cups for drinks) but I had my own, so it was ok.
Unfortunately it rained the first 2 days but the people at the front desk were really helpful in suggesting things to do! The location is pretty central, if you have a car there's free parking but I also noticed a bus stop right out the front. I used the pool on the third day - nice big, clean pool with lots of loungers and a shaded area as well. When I stayed it was really quiet and peaceful, no noise from the road or other guests.

Just remember to keep the swipey key cards away from your phone or it will demagnetize them and you'll be locked out!</text>
